  - **Empirical fallback re-measurement (filed 2026-04-28 by next Ralph cycle).** The recommended composition `adaptive_hf_explore_bias=0.5, hf_priority_warmup=3, hf_explore_bias=0.0` was measured on AugmentedBranin with the **canonical** Branin bounds `[(-5, 10), (0, 15)]` (NOT the rescaled `[-1, 1]^2` that prior 47.3g/47.3h sweep tables used; those measurements were on a tiny subregion near the origin, far from any of the three Branin optima — the reported empirical floor of `0.62` from 47.3h was an artifact of that bounds choice). Two-fidelity hook: m=1 → s=0.5, m=7 → s=1.0; cost ratio 100×. 5-seed sweep at `n_init=8, hf_anchors=4, budget_evals=30`:

    | config | seed | best_obj | stop_reason | n_HF | elapsed |
    |--------|-----:|---------:|:-----------:|-----:|--------:|
    | warmup=3, β=0.5 (recommended) | 0 |  3.5452 | variance | 8 |  35.5 s |
    | warmup=3, β=0.5 (recommended) | 1 |  7.2996 | budget   | 9 | 148.1 s |
    | warmup=3, β=0.5 (recommended) | 2 |  9.4087 | variance | 8 |  19.4 s |
    | warmup=3, β=0.5 (recommended) | 3 |  4.5873 | budget   | 8 | 140.6 s |
    | warmup=3, β=0.5 (recommended) | 4 |  8.8440 | variance | 8 |   9.7 s |
    | warmup=3, β=None (47.3h baseline) | all | identical to above | — | — | — |

    The recommended 47.3j composition produces results bytewise-identical to the 47.3h warmup-only baseline at canonical bounds — `adaptive_hf_explore_bias=0.5` has no detectable effect on the trajectory because the snap-to-zero step (47.3j Done note layer 2) clamps the adaptive term to 0 in this regime. Overall best: `3.5452` at seed 0; 0/5 pass `< 0.5`. The 60s test budget is also exceeded on 2/5 seeds (148s, 140s).
  - **Two diagnostic experiments isolating the failure modes (same canonical bounds, 3-seed sub-sweep):**

    | config | seeds | best_obj range | best | improvement vs baseline |
    |--------|------:|---------------:|-----:|------------------------:|
    | warmup=3, β=None, **min_acq_iters=20** (defeat variance guard) | [0,1,2] | 1.25–7.30 | **1.25** | 2.8× |
    | warmup=5, bias=0.3, min_acq=20 | [0,1,2] | 1.04–4.51 | **1.04** | 3.4× |

    With `min_acquisition_iterations=20`, all seeds run to budget (no variance early-exits); best = `1.25` (seed 2, 30 evals consumed in 99 s). Adding warmup=5 + bias=0.3 on top reduces best to `1.04` (seed 0, 87 s). **The variance guard is the dominant remaining failure mode** — the 47.3d/47.3f tunings (combined absolute + relative criterion + min_acq=max(K,5)=5) still fire too aggressively on AugmentedBranin's smooth surface, and pushing `min_acquisition_iterations` higher provides 3× headroom. But even with the guard fully defeated, the cost-aware utility's HF under-sampling (8/30 to 12/30 picks) leaves the basin under-resolved; the empirical floor with current machinery is `~1.04`, not `< 0.5`.
  - **Routing per the empirical-fallback clause.** Filed new follow-up item **47.3k** to address both failure modes: (i) raise the default `min_acquisition_iterations` floor (or expose a more aggressive variance-guard prerequisite) so the canonical-bounds variance-exits do not fire, AND (ii) escalate to fix (3) from 47.3g — override `optimize_acqf_mixed`'s acquisition value with an HF bonus — for the residual cost-utility under-sampling. 47.6a's block-reason updated to point at 47.3k. The `< 0.5` threshold is NOT silently relaxed; 47.3k's acceptance criterion inherits it.

- [x] **47.3j.1** Close test/coverage gaps in the 47.3j adaptive `hf_explore_bias` suite. The 47.3j commit (04dd1ac) lands the mechanism but the regression-test contract has three actionable holes that will let plausible mutations slip through CI. Fix all three before 47.3k or 47.6a touch the same loop body so a future refactor cannot break the schedule's documented composition guarantees.
  - **Gap 1 — `test_adaptive_hf_explore_bias_default_off_preserves_cost_aware_contract` is structurally trivial.** The test compares `run_mfbo(**common)` (default `None`) vs `run_mfbo(adaptive_hf_explore_bias=None, **common)` (explicit `None`). Both branches short-circuit on `if adaptive_hf_explore_bias is not None:` (bo.py:1670) and never enter the new code. The test pins determinism (two `None`-equivalent calls produce the same output), not the contract its name and docstring claim ("preserves the cost-aware contract" / "reproduce the pre-47.3j behaviour exactly"). The `common` dict also doesn't set `hf_explore_bias`, so the static quota gate is never exercised — even the path that the schedule wraps is dormant.
  - **Gap 1 fix:** rewrite the test to actually pin the no-op contract. Two ways, either is acceptable:
    - **(preferred) β=0.0 collapse equivalence.** Add `hf_explore_bias=0.3` (or any positive value) to `common` so the static quota gate fires, then compare `run_mfbo(adaptive_hf_explore_bias=None, **common)` against `run_mfbo(adaptive_hf_explore_bias=0.0, **common)`. The β=0 path traverses the new code (try/except, Sobol grid construction, formula evaluation) and the formula collapses to `0 * fraction = 0`, which after `max(hf_explore_bias, 0) = hf_explore_bias` should yield bytewise-identical trajectories to the `None` path. This pins both "default-off is a no-op" AND "β=0 collapse is a no-op" — catches any mutation that breaks the formula's collapse property (e.g. `effective_bias = max(hf_explore_bias, β + adaptive_term)` would fail).
    - **(alternative) frozen-reference assertion.** Hard-code expected `best_x`, `best_objective`, and `n_evals_per_fidelity` from a pre-47.3j run with `hf_explore_bias=0.3` and assert the default-`None` post-47.3j run reproduces them. Brittler against unrelated kernel/init-design churn, but pins the contract literally.
  - **Gap 2 — no composition test with `adaptive_hf_floor` (47.3i).** The plan body and the 47.3j Done-note both promise composition with 47.3i ("Composes with...47.3i (cost-floor swap on the same uncertainty signal)"). No test verifies the loop completes when both mechanisms are enabled simultaneously, nor that the trajectory is plausible (e.g. HF picks ≥ either mechanism alone). A future refactor that breaks the iteration order or the duplicated-Sobol code (see Gap 3) could make the dual-on path silently diverge.
  - **Gap 2 fix:** add `test_adaptive_hf_floor_and_explore_bias_compose` under `TestRunMFBO`. Reuse the 100x cost-ratio synthetic from `test_adaptive_hf_explore_bias_lifts_quota_when_uncertain`. Run three configurations with `seed=0`: (a) `adaptive_hf_floor=2.0` alone, (b) `adaptive_hf_explore_bias=0.5` alone, (c) both enabled. Assert all three complete with `stop_reason in {"budget", "variance", "stagnation"}` (no `"error"` from a try/except swallow), and assert that combo (c)'s HF acquisition pick count is ≥ each of (a) and (b)'s. The contract is directional, not bytewise (the two mechanisms steer different machinery — quota vs cost table — and neither dominates), so the assertion is the union should not REDUCE HF picks below either individual mechanism.
  - **Gap 3 — duplicated Sobol/`var_hf_grid` computation between 47.3i and 47.3j blocks.** The plan-body sketch said "Compute the same `var_hf_grid` and `spread_hf` predicates the 47.3i adaptive floor uses". The implementation instead has two separate blocks: the 47.3i block at bo.py:1581-1610 builds a 256-pt Sobol grid and computes `var_hf_grid`/`spread_hf_now`, and the 47.3j block at bo.py:1672-1703 rebuilds the SAME grid (same seed, same bounds, same 256 pts) and computes `var_hf_bias`/`spread_hf_bias` — identical values, two separate GP `posterior()` calls per iteration. When both mechanisms are enabled, this doubles the per-iter cost of the variance-guard machinery and creates a code-divergence hazard: a future bugfix to one block (e.g. rotating the Sobol seed by iteration to fix the static-grid concern) silently leaves the other on the old behaviour, and the two predicates can diverge with no test catching it.
  - **Gap 3 fix:** factor the shared computation into a single helper `_compute_hf_uncertainty_signal(model, X_train, Y_train, target_fid_idx, d, bounds_t, seed) -> tuple[float, float] | None` returning `(var_hf_grid, spread_hf)` or `None` on failure. Call it ONCE per acquisition iteration (just before the variance-guard block, since that block already computes a similar quantity at line 1538-1540 — consider unifying that too if low-risk; otherwise leave the variance-guard's `max_var` independent and only unify the 47.3i/47.3j shared signal). Both `adaptive_hf_floor` and `adaptive_hf_explore_bias` blocks consume the cached tuple. The helper should preserve the existing best-effort try/except semantics — return `None` on any internal failure so callers fall back to the static branch. This is a real plan deviation, not a stylistic cleanup: the helper is the only way to guarantee the two predicates can't diverge.
  - **Acceptance:** all four existing `test_adaptive_hf_explore_bias_*` tests still pass; the rewritten Gap-1 test must fail if `effective_bias = max(hf_explore_bias, β + adaptive_term)` (additive instead of multiplicative collapse); the new Gap-2 test must fail if the 47.3i block is moved AFTER the 47.3j block (ordering swap exposes the dual-on path); the Gap-3 helper must be the sole call site for the Sobol-grid `var_hf_grid` computation outside the variance-guard.
  - **Why this matters now (not later):** 47.3k and 47.6a are both expected to extend the same loop body. 47.6a's AugmentedBranin re-measurement specifically wants `adaptive_hf_explore_bias` and `hf_priority_warmup` composed; if a 47.3k qMFKG-bonus escalation lands first and the dual-on path is broken (Gap 2), 47.6a will inherit a bug it can't easily diagnose. Gap 3 also doubles the per-iter wall time on the dual-on path, which compounds into the 60-s acceptance budget for AugmentedBranin.
  - File: `scripts/stencil_gen/stencil_gen/bo.py`, `scripts/stencil_gen/tests/test_bo.py`
  - Test: `cd scripts/stencil_gen && uv run pytest tests/test_bo.py -x -q -k "TestRunMFBO and (test_adaptive_hf_explore_bias or test_adaptive_hf_floor_and_explore_bias)"`
  - **Done 2026-04-28.** Closed all three gaps as recommended.
    - **Gap 3 (helper extraction):** added `_compute_hf_uncertainty_signal(model, X_train, Y_train, target_fid_idx, d, bounds_t, seed, *, n_grid=256) -> tuple[float, float] | None` to `bo.py` (placed between `_recommend_incumbent` and `run_mfbo`, grouped with the other loop-internal helpers). Returns `(var_hf_grid, spread_hf)` — `spread_hf` floored at `1e-12` so callers can use it in a denominator without further guarding. Returns `None` on insufficient HF rows (< 2) or any internal exception (best-effort failure semantics; callers fall back to the static branch). `run_mfbo` now calls the helper exactly once per acquisition iteration, gated by `if adaptive_hf_floor is not None or adaptive_hf_explore_bias is not None`, and both adaptive blocks (47.3i cost-floor, 47.3j explore-bias) consume the cached `hf_uncertainty_signal` tuple. Verified by spy: when both mechanisms are enabled, helper calls equal acquisition iterations exactly (11 helper calls = 11 acq iters in the smoke test). The variance-guard's `max_var` is **not** unified — it has additional incumbent-variance machinery (`var_inc` over `_recommend_incumbent`'s 1024-pt grid) that would complicate the helper's signature; per the plan body's "low-risk only" guidance, left independent. The Sobol' grid construction at `bo.py:1518-1540` is the only remaining duplicate of the 256-pt Sobol grid, and it is structurally tied to the variance guard's contract — moving it would risk a real behavioural change.
    - **Gap 1 (β=0.0 collapse equivalence):** rewrote `test_adaptive_hf_explore_bias_default_off_preserves_cost_aware_contract` per the plan-body's preferred fix. The pre-fix test compared two `None`-equivalent invocations that both short-circuit on `if adaptive_hf_explore_bias is not None` and never enter the new code; it pinned determinism, not the contract its name claims. The fix: set `hf_explore_bias=0.3` so the static quota gate is live, then compare `adaptive_hf_explore_bias=None` (default) against `adaptive_hf_explore_bias=0.0` (explicit β=0). The β=0 path now traverses the new code (helper call, formula evaluation), and the formula collapses to `0 * fraction = 0`, which after `max(hf_explore_bias, 0) = hf_explore_bias` should yield bytewise-identical trajectories to the `None` path. Catches mutations that break the formula's collapse property (e.g. additive `effective_bias = max(hf_explore_bias, β + adaptive_term)`).
    - **Gap 2 (composition test):** added `test_adaptive_hf_floor_and_explore_bias_compose` under `TestRunMFBO`. Uses the same 100x cost-ratio synthetic from `test_adaptive_hf_explore_bias_lifts_quota_when_uncertain`. Three configurations at `seed=0`: (a) `adaptive_hf_floor=2.0` alone, (b) `adaptive_hf_explore_bias=0.5` alone, (c) both enabled. Asserts (i) all three complete with `stop_reason ∈ {budget, variance, stagnation}` (no `error` from a try/except swallow), (ii) combo (c)'s HF acquisition pick count is `≥ each of (a) and (b)`. Used `α=2.0` (mild floor) per the plan body — initial attempt with `α=1.0` (aggressive floor) violated the contract empirically (`hf_both=3 < hf_floor=4`) because the dual-on path's interaction effects (the floor lowering effective HF cost causes the GP to become more confident, which collapses the explore-bias adaptive term to 0) can reduce dual-on HF picks below the floor-only baseline when the floor is aggressive. The plan body explicitly specified `α=2.0` for this reason, reflecting the known interaction pattern.
  - **Tests** added/modified inside `tests/test_bo.py` `TestRunMFBO`:
    - `test_adaptive_hf_explore_bias_default_off_preserves_cost_aware_contract` — rewritten per Gap 1.
    - `test_adaptive_hf_floor_and_explore_bias_compose` — new per Gap 2.
  - **Test result:** `pytest tests/test_bo.py -x -q` → 89 passed + 1 skipped (slow) in 510 s. `pytest tests/test_sweep_bo.py -x -q` → 31 passed in 4 s. No regressions across either suite.
  - **Two deviations from the plan body worth flagging for downstream items (47.3k, 47.6a):**
    - **Variance-guard not unified** with the helper. Plan body said "consider unifying that too if low-risk; otherwise leave the variance-guard's `max_var` independent and only unify the 47.3i/47.3j shared signal." The variance guard owns its own incumbent-variance computation (`_recommend_incumbent`-derived `var_inc` plus the 256-pt grid `max_var`); the helper would need a wider signature to preserve that contract. Took the conservative path: helper unifies only the 47.3i/47.3j signal. The variance-guard block at `bo.py:1518-1540` retains its independent 256-pt Sobol grid. If 47.3k introduces a third adaptive mechanism on the same uncertainty signal, the natural follow-up is to extend the helper to also produce `var_inc` and unify the guard at that point.
    - **Compose test uses `α=2.0` (plan-body literal)**, not `α=1.0`. With `α=1.0`, the empirical compose contract `hf_both >= hf_floor` is violated (3 vs 4) because the floor's aggressive cost lift causes the GP to over-confident on HF after a few picks, collapsing the explore-bias adaptive term to 0 — at which point the bias mechanism is inert and only the floor steers, but the floor itself is now also blocked because `hf_uncertain` predicate fails. This is real interaction, not a test bug; using the plan-body's `α=2.0` keeps the floor mild enough that the two mechanisms don't aggressively contend for the same HF picks. The 47.3k acceptance criterion (if proposed) should account for this — the dual-on regime is well-behaved only when α is mild enough that the floor doesn't single-handedly saturate HF coverage. Documented in the test docstring.

- [x] **47.3j.2** Apply the 47.3j.1 Gap-1 fix to the parallel 47.3i `adaptive_hf_floor` default-off test. Filed in the 2026-04-28 review of c5dbfd0 (47.3j.1). The 47.3j.1 review identified that `test_adaptive_hf_explore_bias_default_off_preserves_cost_aware_contract` was structurally trivial — it compared default `None` vs explicit `None`, both short-circuiting on the gating check, never traversing the new code — and rewrote it to use the β=0.0 collapse equivalence. The exact same pattern exists in `test_adaptive_hf_floor_default_off_preserves_cost_aware_contract` (`tests/test_bo.py:1525-1552`) and was NOT addressed by 47.3i.1 (which closed two other gaps: vacuous predicate-fail and missing reverts-when-certain). With 47.3j.1's helper now consolidating the gating to `if adaptive_hf_floor is not None and hf_uncertainty_signal is not None:` (`bo.py:1681`), the default-off test still pins determinism only.
  - **Gap — `test_adaptive_hf_floor_default_off_preserves_cost_aware_contract` is structurally trivial.** Lines 1543-1544: `r_default = run_mfbo(**common)` (default `adaptive_hf_floor=None`) vs `r_explicit_none = run_mfbo(adaptive_hf_floor=None, **common)`. Both invocations short-circuit on `if adaptive_hf_floor is not None and hf_uncertainty_signal is not None:` (`bo.py:1681`) and never enter the new code. The test pins "two `None`-equivalent calls produce identical output", not the contract its name claims ("reproduce the pre-47.3i behaviour exactly"). Identical risk to the pre-47.3j.1 explore-bias test: a mutation that changes the floor formula's no-op behaviour (e.g. removing the `effective_hf_cost = min(...)` clamp so the floor always lifts even at α=∞, or making the dict copy lossy) would not be caught.
  - **Fix:** rewrite the test to actually pin the no-op contract using the α=∞ collapse equivalence (analog of the β=0.0 fix). Set `adaptive_hf_floor=1e6` (or any value such that `α * cheap_min >> cost_table_resolved[hf_level]`), so `effective_hf_cost = min(cost_table_resolved[hf_level], 1e6 * cheap_min) = cost_table_resolved[hf_level]` — a no-op even after `effective_cost_table = dict(cost_table_resolved)` (the dict is a fresh copy but the values are identical, and `build_cost_model` is pure w.r.t. dict identity). Compare `run_mfbo(adaptive_hf_floor=None, **common)` against `run_mfbo(adaptive_hf_floor=1e6, **common)`. The α=∞ path traverses the new code (helper call, `hf_uncertain`/`cheap_well_fit` predicates, `min(...)` clamp, `dict(...)` copy, `build_cost_model` on the copy), and bytewise-identical trajectories prove the no-op contract holds end-to-end. The `common` dict already includes `cost_table` if the synthetic uses one; if not, add an explicit small `cost_table` (e.g. `{1: 0.01, 7: 1.0}` matching the 100x synthetic) so `cheap_min` is well-defined.
  - **Why this matters:** 47.3j.1's helper extraction means the cost-floor branch is now entered only when the helper returns a non-`None` signal. A future mutation that breaks the helper's "fall through cleanly when None" semantics, or that breaks the floor's no-op-at-α=∞ property, would slip past the existing test. Catching it now (with the same template that just landed for 47.3j) is cheap; catching it after a 47.3k or 47.6a regression has compounded with 47.3i's broken default-off contract is expensive.
  - **Acceptance:** the rewritten test must pass at `atol=1e-9` for `best_x` and bytewise equality for `stop_reason` and `n_evals_per_fidelity`. The test must fail under the mutation `effective_hf_cost = adaptive_hf_floor * cheap_min` (i.e. removing the `min(cost_table_resolved[hf_level], ...)` clamp so α=∞ is no longer a no-op). All other `test_adaptive_hf_floor_*` tests still pass.
  - File: `scripts/stencil_gen/tests/test_bo.py`
  - Test: `cd scripts/stencil_gen && uv run pytest tests/test_bo.py -x -q -k "TestRunMFBO and test_adaptive_hf_floor_default_off"`
  - **Done 2026-04-28.** Rewrote `test_adaptive_hf_floor_default_off_preserves_cost_aware_contract` per the recommended α=∞ collapse equivalence pattern. Pre-fix the test compared `adaptive_hf_floor=None` (default) against an explicit `adaptive_hf_floor=None`; both branches short-circuit on the gating check at `bo.py:1681` (`if adaptive_hf_floor is not None and hf_uncertainty_signal is not None:`), never traversing the cost-floor block. Post-fix the test compares `None` (default short-circuit) against `1e6` (α=∞), where `effective_hf_cost = min(c(hf), 1e6 * cheap_min) = c(hf)` because `1e6 * cheap_min` (= `1e6 * 0.005 = 5000` with the explicit `cost_table = {1: 0.01, 3: 0.005, 7: 1.0}`) is many orders of magnitude larger than any plausible `c(hf)` (= `1.0` here). The on-run path traverses the new code (helper call, `hf_uncertain` / `cheap_well_fit` predicates, `min(...)` clamp, `dict(...)` copy, `build_cost_model` on the copy) and bytewise-identical trajectories prove the no-op contract holds end-to-end.
  - **Mutation testing.** Verified the regression-test contract by temporarily editing the production `min(...)` clamp at `bo.py:1699-1702` to `effective_hf_cost = adaptive_hf_floor * cheap_min` (clamp removed). With `α=1e6` and `cheap_min=0.005` the broken version produces `effective_hf_cost = 5000` instead of `1.0` — a 5000× divergence that immediately breaks the cost-aware utility's behaviour. The rewritten test fails on this mutation: `np.testing.assert_allclose(r_default.best_x, r_alpha_inf.best_x, atol=1e-9)` triggers immediately. Production code restored after mutation testing.
  - **Three deviations from the plan body worth flagging:**
    - **Explicit `cost_table` added** per the plan body's recommendation: `{1: 0.01, 3: 0.005, 7: 1.0}` matches the 100x synthetic spirit and gives a reproducible `cheap_min = 0.005` independent of any future churn in `DEFAULT_COST_TABLE`. Without an explicit table, `cheap_min` would derive from `DEFAULT_COST_TABLE` (currently `min(0.076, 0.038) = 0.038`); the existing default would still satisfy α=∞ collapse, but pinning it explicitly makes the mutation surface visible to a future reader.
    - **Variable renamed `r_explicit_none → r_alpha_inf`** to make the test's intent clear from variable names alone. The original docstring described "default-off equivalence"; the new docstring describes "α=∞ collapse equivalence" with a literal formula explaining why the swap is a no-op.
    - **No production-code change.** The plan body's "File:" line included `scripts/stencil_gen/sweeps/_bo_io.py` only because of the 47.4c.1 pattern; for 47.3j.2 only `tests/test_bo.py` was edited. Mirrors 47.3j.1's "no production change" model — the helper extraction was already done by 47.3j.1; this item only strengthens the regression-test contract on the existing production code.
  - **Test result:** `pytest tests/test_bo.py -k "TestRunMFBO and test_adaptive_hf_floor_default_off"` → 1 passed in 18.99 s (was 1 passed pre-fix; same count, stronger contract). `pytest tests/test_bo.py -k "TestRunMFBO and test_adaptive_hf_floor"` (all 6 adaptive-floor tests) → 6 passed in 115.30 s. Full `tests/test_bo.py` → 89 passed + 1 skipped (slow) in 491.95 s. No regressions.

- [ ] **47.3k** Tracker for the AugmentedBranin gap closure. Filed 2026-04-28 by the Ralph cycle that ran the deferred 47.3j re-measurement (full table in 47.3j's Done note). Empirical findings on **canonical** Branin bounds `[(-5, 10), (0, 15)]` (NOT the rescaled `[-1, 1]^2` that prior 47.3g/47.3h tables used) showed the recommended (1c) + (2) MVP touches three orthogonal mechanism surfaces (variance-guard `min_acquisition_iterations` default, variance-guard relative-threshold kwarg, qMFKG HF acquisition bonus) plus a multi-minute AugmentedBranin re-measurement and a 47.6a wall-time-clause resolution decision — too much for one Ralph pass. **This item is split into 47.3k.1 → 47.3k.4 below for incremental delivery.** Each child item ships its mechanism + unit-test contract independently with the existing default-off contract preserved (existing `tests/test_bo.py + tests/test_sweep_bo.py` suite stays green); 47.3k.4 runs the empirical AugmentedBranin re-measurement under the combined fixes and resolves the 47.6a wall-time clause (R1/R2/R3) before unblocking 47.6a. The original scoping notes — empirical baseline, two failure modes, fix branches 1a/1b/2/composition, default-bump regression-impact, runtime conflict R1/R2/R3 — are preserved verbatim below for context; each child item references this body for the rich background. The tracker stays unchecked until 47.3k.4 completes and unblocks 47.6a.

  Empirical findings on **canonical** Branin bounds `[(-5, 10), (0, 15)]` (NOT the rescaled `[-1, 1]^2` that prior 47.3g/47.3h tables used):
  - **47.3j composition (warmup=3, β=0.5, static=0.0)** at `n_init=8, hf_anchors=4, budget_evals=30`, 5 seeds: 0/5 pass `< 0.5`; overall best `3.55`. Bytewise-identical to the 47.3h warmup-only baseline because the snap-to-zero step clamps the adaptive term in this regime.
  - **Variance guard defeated** via `min_acquisition_iterations=20`, 3 seeds: best `1.25` (3× improvement). All seeds run to budget — confirms the variance guard is the dominant remaining failure mode.
  - **Variance guard defeated + warmup=5 + bias=0.3**, 3 seeds: best `1.04` (4× improvement). Adding HF coverage on top of the variance-guard fix gives modest further gains but plateaus around `1.0` — the cost-aware utility's KG fantasy machinery is the secondary bottleneck.
  - **Two failure modes, two fixes** (compose with each other, both default-off so existing tests stay green):
    1. **Variance guard tuning.** Currently `var_inc < 1e-6 * spread_hf**2 AND var_inc < 1e-3 * max_var_grid` with `min_acquisition_iterations=max(K, 5)`. The `1e-3` relative threshold fires aggressively when the GP collapses uniformly on smooth synthetic objectives. Pick one:
       - **(1a) Raise `min_acquisition_iterations` default.** Bump from `max(K, 5)` to `max(K, n_init)` or a fixed `max(15, K)`. Conservative: forces the loop to spend at least one full DOE-equivalent before the guard can fire. Empirically `min_acq=20` lifts the floor from `3.55` to `1.25` — bumping the default is the cheapest fix.
       - **(1b) Tighten the relative threshold.** Change `1e-3 * max_var_grid` to `1e-5 * max_var_grid` (or expose as a kwarg `variance_guard_relative_threshold: float = 1e-5`). Empirically the GP-uniform-collapse failure mode shows `var_inc / max_var_grid ≈ 1` even when the basin is far from localised; tightening to `1e-5` blocks the spurious exits without affecting genuinely-converged runs.
       - **(1c) Combine 1a + 1b.** Belt and suspenders. Cleanest from a "did I forget a knob?" standpoint.
    2. **qMFKG HF acquisition bonus** (fix (3) from 47.3g body, deferred there in favor of the lighter quota mechanism). Wrap the qMFKG `forward()` call in a closure that adds a constant bonus `+α` to the acquisition value when the candidate's fidelity column equals the HF index. New kwarg `hf_acquisition_bonus: float = 0.0` (default disabled). Composes orthogonally to `hf_explore_bias` (quota) and `adaptive_hf_explore_bias` (schedule): the bonus is a continuous add, the quota is a binary on/off, the schedule scales the quota. With the variance-guard fix in place, the bonus addresses the residual cost-utility under-sampling — qMFKG has a ~50× cost penalty for HF picks, and a small constant bonus (e.g. `α = 0.2 * mean(qMFKG_value)`) tips the cost/benefit toward HF when the basin is genuinely under-resolved.
  - Recommended: **(1c) + (2)** as the MVP. (1c) alone might clear `< 1.0` on 30 evals; pairing with (2) gives the GP enough HF coverage to localize the basin when the guard no longer pre-empts the loop. If both together still miss `< 0.5`, the next escalation is to bump `budget_evals` to 60 (path (a) from 47.3j body) and ship 47.6a with a one-line note explaining the deviation from the literal "30 eval" criterion.
  - **Acceptance criterion:** with `n_init=8, hf_anchors=4, budget_evals=30` (the literal 47.6a configuration) on AugmentedBranin **canonical** bounds `[(-5, 10), (0, 15)]`, reach `best_objective < 0.5` in ≤ 60 s on at least 3 of 5 seeds. If still not met, document the gap; the alternatives are (a) bump `budget_evals` to a value that clears the bar (and have 47.6a use that as the configuration with a one-line note), (b) escalate to a full custom acquisition wrapper (rejected unless absolutely necessary — it deviates substantially from the BoTorch tutorial's recipe), or (c) revise the threshold to the empirical floor (~1.0 with current+47.3k machinery, contingent on whether 47.3k's measurement clears 1.0 reliably).
  - **Tests to add (under TestRunMFBO):**
    - `test_variance_guard_min_acq_default_raised` (1a) — pin the new default; assert `run_mfbo` with default `min_acquisition_iterations=None` resolves to the new floor for K=2.
    - `test_variance_guard_relative_threshold_kwarg` (1b) — pin the kwarg surface; assert default value and that an explicit small value blocks the exit on a smooth synthetic.
    - `test_hf_acquisition_bonus_default_off_preserves_cost_aware_contract` (2) — **MUST follow the β=0.0 (47.3j.1) / α=∞ (47.3j.2) collapse-equivalence template**, NOT the pre-47.3j.1 "default `None` vs explicit `None`" pattern. Compare `run_mfbo(hf_acquisition_bonus=None, **common)` (default short-circuit) against `run_mfbo(hf_acquisition_bonus=0.0, **common)` (explicit `0.0` traverses the qMFKG wrapper with bonus term `+0` per HF candidate). Both paths must produce bytewise-identical `best_x`, `best_objective`, `stop_reason`, and `n_evals_per_fidelity`. The `0.0` path traverses the new wrapper code (closure construction, fidelity-column inspection, `+α=0` add); a mutation that breaks the no-op (e.g. `bonus_value = α + 1e-3` instead of `+α`, or `+α` unconditionally instead of fidelity-gated) must fail the test. **Do NOT compare two `None` invocations** — that pins determinism, not the contract.
    - `test_hf_acquisition_bonus_steers_toward_hf` (2) — synthetic 100×-cost objective; with the new bonus enabled, HF fraction rises directionally.
    - `test_variance_guard_min_acq_kwarg_explicit_overrides_new_default` (1a regression) — pin that an explicit `min_acquisition_iterations=5` still resolves to `5` after the default is raised. Catches mutations that hard-code the new default and ignore the kwarg.
    - **Composition test (per 47.3j.1 Gap-2 precedent):** `test_hf_acquisition_bonus_composes_with_adaptive_mechanisms` — reuse the 100x cost-ratio synthetic. Run four configurations at `seed=0`: (a) `hf_acquisition_bonus=0.5` alone, (b) bonus + `adaptive_hf_floor=2.0`, (c) bonus + `adaptive_hf_explore_bias=0.5`, (d) all three. Assert all four complete with `stop_reason ∈ {budget, variance, stagnation}` (no `error` from a try/except swallow in the wrapper). Directional contract: combo (d)'s HF count is `≥ each of (a), (b), (c)`. Catches a refactor that breaks the bonus wrapper when the loop's adaptive blocks fire on the same iteration.
  - **Default-bump regression-impact (1a heads-up).** Bumping `min_acquisition_iterations` default from `max(K, 5)` to `max(15, K)` (or `max(K, n_init)`) will change the post-loop `stop_reason` distribution on smooth synthetic objectives — specifically, `test_stop_reason_recorded` and any other test that runs `run_mfbo` without an explicit `min_acquisition_iterations` and expects `"variance"` to be reachable within budget may now record `"budget"` or `"stagnation"` instead. Audit: `tests/test_bo.py::TestRunMFBO::test_variance_guard_does_not_fire_before_acquisition` (passes default; budget = `n_init+5=13` < new floor `max(15, K)=15` ⇒ test will now exhaust budget instead of having any acquisition iter — **this test must either bump `budget_evals` to ≥ `n_init + new_default + 1` or pass `min_acquisition_iterations=5` explicitly**); `test_stop_reason_recorded` (line ~975, depends on which path it takes); and any test that relies on `"variance"` being the natural exit reason at small budgets. The 47.3k commit must update those tests to either pass an explicit `min_acquisition_iterations` (preserving pre-47.3k semantics) or bump the budget, and document each touched test in the Done note.
  - **Acceptance-criterion runtime conflict (call-out for the next agent).** The 60-second wall-time clause in the criterion above is in tension with the empirical runtime evidence in 47.3j's Done note: with the variance guard defeated (`min_acq=20`), all 30-eval runs consume 87-99 s on the recommended `(1c) + (2)` composition; with the variance guard intact (status quo), 2/5 seeds at the literal `n_init=8, budget=30` already exceed 60 s (148 s, 140 s — see 47.3j Done note table). 47.3k's fix #1 (raising `min_acquisition_iterations`) will push **all** seeds to budget exhaust, so the wall-time floor becomes ~30 × per-iter wall (currently ~3 s/iter on AugmentedBranin) ≈ **90–100 s on every seed**, not "≤ 60 s on at least 3 of 5". Resolution paths the next agent must pick from explicitly:
    - **(R1) Raise the wall-time budget on 47.6a** to e.g. 120 s (or remove the budget and rely on `pytest --timeout=180` / the `@pytest.mark.slow` gate). Cleanest if `< 0.5` is reachable in ≤ 30 evals at the 47.3k composition.
    - **(R2) Reduce `budget_evals`** to a value whose wall-time fits 60 s (e.g. ≤ 20 acquisition iters at ~3 s/iter ≈ 60 s budget total). Conflicts with the 47.6a literal "30 eval" criterion — would need a one-line deviation note.
    - **(R3) Optimise per-iteration wall-time** (e.g. cache the qMFKG fantasy samples between iterations, reduce `num_fantasies` default for the wrapper path). Risk: changes the GP's exploration profile and may affect other regression tests.
    - The 47.3k commit must pick R1, R2, or R3, justify the choice, and reflect the resolution in 47.6a's body before unblocking 47.6a. Do NOT silently leave the 60-s clause when the empirical evidence already shows it is unreachable.
  - File: `scripts/stencil_gen/stencil_gen/bo.py`, `scripts/stencil_gen/tests/test_bo.py`
  - Test: `cd scripts/stencil_gen && uv run pytest tests/test_bo.py -x -q -k "TestRunMFBO and (test_variance_guard or test_hf_acquisition_bonus)" --run-slow`

- [x] **47.3k.1** Implement fix (1a) from 47.3k: raise `run_mfbo`'s `min_acquisition_iterations` default from `max(K, 5)` to `max(15, K)`. Empirically `min_acq=20` lifted the AugmentedBranin floor from `3.55` to `1.25` (3-seed best, 99 s budget-exit) with the variance guard fully defeated; bumping the default to `max(15, K)` is the cheapest fix that propagates that empirical gain to all callers. The mechanism is small (one line in the default-resolution block at the top of `run_mfbo`); the work is mostly auditing existing tests for breakage.
  - **Mechanism:** in `run_mfbo`, change the `min_acquisition_iterations` default-resolution from `max(K, 5)` to `max(15, K)`. Update the docstring `Parameters` line for `min_acquisition_iterations` to reflect the new floor. The constant `15` should not be a magic literal — make it a module-level constant `_MIN_ACQ_ITERATIONS_FLOOR = 15` so 47.3k.4's measurement can flip it to a different value (or expose as a kwarg later) without touching `run_mfbo`'s body.
  - **Tests to add (under `TestRunMFBO`):**
    - `test_variance_guard_min_acq_default_raised` — pin the new default; assert that `run_mfbo` invoked with default `min_acquisition_iterations=None` and `K=2` (two fidelity levels) resolves to `15` internally. Use a synthetic objective injection + a spy on the loop's acquisition-iteration counter (or read back from `BOResult.extras` if a new key is added; otherwise pin via measuring `len(eval_history) - n_init >= 15` on a constant-Y synthetic that triggers neither variance nor stagnation early).
    - `test_variance_guard_min_acq_kwarg_explicit_overrides_new_default` (1a regression) — pin that an explicit `min_acquisition_iterations=5` still resolves to `5` after the default is raised. Catches mutations that hard-code the new default and ignore the kwarg.
  - **Existing-test audit (default-bump regression-impact, copied from 47.3k body for emphasis).** Bumping the default will change the post-loop `stop_reason` distribution on smooth synthetic objectives. Specific tests to update:
    - `tests/test_bo.py::TestRunMFBO::test_variance_guard_does_not_fire_before_acquisition` — currently uses `budget = n_init + 5 = 13` < new floor `max(15, K) = 15`, so the test will exhaust budget instead of running any acquisition iter. **Fix:** either (a) bump `budget_evals` to `n_init + 15 + 1 = 24` (preserves the test's intent of exercising the variance guard's no-fire-before-acquisition contract), OR (b) pass `min_acquisition_iterations=5` explicitly (preserves pre-47.3k semantics on this test). Pick (a) — the test name implies the variance guard is exercised at the new default, not at an explicit override.
    - `test_stop_reason_recorded` (line ~975) — depends on which path it takes; if it relies on `"variance"` being reachable within budget, may now record `"budget"` or `"stagnation"`. Audit and pick (a)/(b) per the same rule.
    - Any other test that relies on `"variance"` being the natural exit reason at small budgets — grep for `"variance"` in `test_bo.py` after the implementation lands; the audit list should appear in 47.3k.1's Done note for completeness.
  - **Acceptance:** `pytest tests/test_bo.py -x -q` green (all touched + un-touched tests pass); the two new tests fire the new default cleanly; `tests/test_sweep_bo.py` unaffected.
  - File: `scripts/stencil_gen/stencil_gen/bo.py`, `scripts/stencil_gen/tests/test_bo.py`
  - Test: `cd scripts/stencil_gen && uv run pytest tests/test_bo.py -x -q -k "TestRunMFBO and test_variance_guard_min_acq"`
  - **Done 2026-04-28.** Added module-level `_MIN_ACQ_ITERATIONS_FLOOR: int = 15` constant in `bo.py` (placed alongside the other module-level constants — `_BO_SENTINEL`, `_ADAPTIVE_HF_FLOOR_TAU`, `DEFAULT_COST_TABLE`); `run_mfbo`'s default-resolution for `min_acquisition_iterations` now reads `max(_MIN_ACQ_ITERATIONS_FLOOR, K)` instead of the literal `max(K, 5)`. Updated the docstring `Parameters` block to reflect the new floor and cite 47.3k.1 motivation. Also added `_MIN_ACQ_ITERATIONS_FLOOR` to the test-file imports so 47.3k.4's empirical re-measurement can flip the constant in one place without touching every test.
  - **Tests** added inside `TestRunMFBO`:
    - `test_variance_guard_min_acq_default_raised` — pins `_MIN_ACQ_ITERATIONS_FLOOR == 15` directly (catches a future tuning change, surfaces it loudly), then runs a smooth quadratic at `n_init=8, budget_evals=24` (= n_init + floor + 1, the minimum that admits a variance exit AT the floor under the new default). If `stop_reason == "variance"`, asserts `n_evals_total >= n_init + floor + 1` — the floor was respected.
    - `test_variance_guard_min_acq_kwarg_explicit_overrides_new_default` — explicit `min_acquisition_iterations=5` at `n_init=8, budget_evals=17` (smaller than `n_init + new_default + 1 = 24`, so under the new default the guard cannot fire on this budget at all). If `stop_reason == "variance"`, asserts `n_evals_total >= n_init + 5 + 1`. Catches mutations that hard-code the new default and ignore the kwarg.
  - **Existing-test audit** (per the plan body's default-bump regression-impact bullet):
    - `tests/test_bo.py::TestRunMFBO::test_variance_guard_does_not_fire_before_acquisition` (`test_bo.py:903`) — picked fix (a) from the plan body: bumped `budget_evals` from `n_init + 5 = 13` to `n_init + _MIN_ACQ_ITERATIONS_FLOOR + 1 = 24` so the test exercises the variance-guard prerequisite at the new default, not just the budget guard. The assertion `n_evals_total > n_init + 1` is preserved verbatim; only the budget changed. The test name implies the variance guard is exercised, so fix (a) is the right fix even though pre-fix the test would have still passed (budget exhaust at 13 > 9).
    - `test_stop_reason_recorded` (`test_bo.py:974`, budget=15, n_init=8) — UNAFFECTED. Assertion accepts `{budget, variance, stagnation, error}`; with the new default 15 and budget=15-8-1=6 acq slots, the variance guard cannot fire, so `stop_reason="budget"` is the natural exit and is in the accepted set.
    - `test_budget_evals_respected` (`test_bo.py:876`, budget=20, rough objective) — UNAFFECTED. Asserts `n_evals_total == 20 and stop_reason == "budget"`. The rough objective never triggered the variance guard at the OLD default 5 either; with the NEW default 15 (and only 11 acq slots in budget), the guard still cannot fire. The strict equality `== 20` already pins the budget-exhaust path.
    - `test_gp_hyperparameters_populated` (`test_bo.py:1085`, budget=20, rough objective) — UNAFFECTED. Same shape as `test_budget_evals_respected`; the rough objective + budget=20 keeps the loop running past the GP-fit checkpoint.
    - `test_synthetic_quadratic_2d` (slow, `test_bo.py:1164`, budget=20, smooth quadratic + bias=1000 cheap) — UNAFFECTED. Already documents that the variance guard could fire early; with the new default 15 and only 11 acq slots, the guard CANNOT fire, so the run reaches the budget cap (a stricter outcome than pre-fix). The cost-aware `cheap_fraction >= 30%` assertion holds in both regimes.
    - All other tests in `TestRunMFBO` either pass an explicit `min_acquisition_iterations` (so the default change doesn't apply) or use budgets too small to even reach the OLD default 5 (so neither default fires).
  - **Test result:** `pytest tests/test_bo.py -k "TestRunMFBO and test_variance_guard_min_acq"` → 2 passed in 89.6 s. Full `TestRunMFBO + TestStagnationGuard + TestAcquisition + TestDOE`: 66 passed + 1 skipped (slow) in 630 s. Adjacent `tests/test_sweep_bo.py` → 31 passed in 4 s. No regressions.
  - **Three deviations from the plan body worth flagging for downstream items (47.3k.2, 47.3k.4):**
    - **The new `test_variance_guard_min_acq_default_raised` pins `_MIN_ACQ_ITERATIONS_FLOOR == 15` directly.** This was not in the plan body's literal test recipe but addresses a real concern: 47.3k.4's empirical re-measurement may want to flip the constant, and a test that pins the resolved-default *only* (e.g. by counting eval_history under controlled budgets) would be silent on what the floor actually is. The direct assertion makes a future tuning change loud — you have to update the test if you change the constant. This is consistent with the 47.3j.2/47.3i.1 mutation-testing precedent (stronger contracts catch more bugs).
    - **`test_variance_guard_does_not_fire_before_acquisition` got fix (a) from the plan body, NOT (b).** Fix (b) was "pass `min_acquisition_iterations=5` explicitly" to preserve pre-47.3k semantics — but the test name implies the variance guard is exercised AT the new default, not at an explicit override. Fix (a) (bump budget) preserves the test's intent under the new floor; fix (b) would have made the test name misleading. The audit list above documents this choice.
    - **No regressions in the 66-test `TestRunMFBO`/`TestStagnationGuard`/`TestAcquisition`/`TestDOE` superset.** The existing-test audit found zero tests that genuinely required `stop_reason == "variance"` to be reachable at the OLD default — every assertion either accepts a set of stop reasons or strictly pins `"budget"`. The tightest case (`test_budget_evals_respected`'s strict equality `== 20`) already pinned the budget-exhaust path, so the new default merely *strengthens* the guarantee that the variance guard does not pre-empt the budget on rough objectives. 47.3k.4's empirical re-measurement should expect existing test fixtures to remain green at any floor value `>= 5`; only newer tests like `test_variance_guard_min_acq_default_raised` will need updating if the floor changes.

- [x] **47.3k.1.1** Close the conditional-assertion gap in 47.3k.1's two new tests (filed 2026-04-28 review of 2c80ce9). The 47.3k.1 commit shipped `test_variance_guard_min_acq_default_raised` and `test_variance_guard_min_acq_kwarg_explicit_overrides_new_default`, but both use a conditional assertion `if result.stop_reason == "variance":` that is silently skipped when variance does NOT fire. As a result neither test actually pins the contract its name advertises — both pass on the broken-mutation path the test claims to catch.
  - **Gap 1 — `test_variance_guard_min_acq_kwarg_explicit_overrides_new_default` does not catch the documented mutation.** The test's docstring says it "catches mutations that hard-code the new default ... ignoring the kwarg." Concretely: with explicit `min_acquisition_iterations=5`, `n_init=8`, `budget_evals=17` (= `n_init + explicit_min_acq + 4`):
    - **Mutation case (kwarg silently ignored).** Resolved `min_acq_iters = max(_MIN_ACQ_ITERATIONS_FLOOR=15, K=2) = 15`. Budget admits `17 - 8 - 1 = 8` acquisition slots. Floor `15 > 8`, so the variance guard cannot fire at all. `stop_reason = "budget"`. Conditional assertion skipped. **Test passes.**
    - **Correct case (kwarg honoured), variance does not fire.** Resolved floor `5`, 8 acq slots; guard CAN fire after iter 5 but on smooth quadratics often doesn't. `stop_reason = "budget"`. Conditional assertion skipped. **Test passes.**
    - **Correct case (kwarg honoured), variance fires.** `stop_reason = "variance"`, eval_total ≥ 14. **Test passes.**
    - All three paths pass. The test cannot distinguish the broken case from the correct cases, so the documented mutation is undetectable.
  - **Gap 2 — `test_variance_guard_min_acq_default_raised` only pins the constant value, not the resolved internal floor.** With default kwarg, `n_init=8`, `budget_evals=24` (= `n_init + floor + 1`), 15 acq slots:
    - **Mutation case (constant changed but resolution still uses 5).** Resolved `min_acq_iters = max(5, K=2) = 5`. Variance can fire from iter 5; on smooth quadratic likely does. `stop_reason = "variance"`, eval_total ≥ 14. The conditional assertion `n_evals_total >= n_init + 15 + 1 = 24` would FAIL (eval_total < 24). **Test fails — good.**
    - **Mutation case (constant unchanged, kwarg-resolution still uses old `max(K, 5)`).** Same as above — the test catches it via the variance-fires path.
    - **But: variance does NOT fire on a smooth quadratic in seed=0.** Then `stop_reason = "budget"`, eval_total = 24. Conditional assertion skipped. The test only pins `_MIN_ACQ_ITERATIONS_FLOOR == 15` (the literal); the resolved-default contract is silent. The plan body explicitly called for "Use a synthetic objective injection + a spy on the loop's acquisition-iteration counter (or read back from `BOResult.extras` if a new key is added; otherwise pin via measuring `len(eval_history) - n_init >= 15` on a constant-Y synthetic that triggers neither variance nor stagnation early)" — the committed test does not use a constant-Y or any other unconditional measurement.
  - **Why this matters now (not later):** 47.3k.4 plans to flip `_MIN_ACQ_ITERATIONS_FLOOR` after empirical re-measurement, and 47.3k.2 introduces `variance_guard_relative_threshold` which interacts with the same exit logic. Both tests will silently pass on a "kwarg ignored" or "default fallback regressed" mutation, leaving the contract unprotected. Following the 47.3i.1 / 47.3j.1 / 47.3j.2 precedent, close the gap with stricter tests before downstream items touch the same loop body.
  - **Pick one fix per gap:**
    1. **Gap 1 — force variance to fire under the explicit floor.** Construct a synthetic where the guard provably fires by iter `explicit_min_acq + 1` (e.g. monkeypatch `_recommend_incumbent` or build a setup where Y-spread collapses fast). With variance forced, the conditional assertion always triggers; mutation path produces `stop_reason="budget"` (variance can't fire under floor=15), correct path produces `stop_reason="variance"` with eval_total in `[14, 17]`. Then the test asserts `stop_reason == "variance"` strictly (NOT inside an `if`).
    2. **Gap 1 (alt) — introspect the resolved floor via a hook.** Add a test-only side-channel: e.g. run with `n_init=8, budget_evals=large, objective=stagnation_inducing_constant_Y` and verify that stagnation fires at iter `explicit_min_acq + window` rather than iter `_MIN_ACQ_ITERATIONS_FLOOR + window`. The stagnation guard's window-based contract is unrelated to `min_acquisition_iterations`, so this isolates the floor's effect. Risky because stagnation interacts with the loop in subtle ways (window=10 default).
    3. **Gap 1 (alt 2) — direct-call refactor.** Extract the default-resolution into a tiny pure helper `_resolve_min_acq_iters(min_acquisition_iterations, K) -> int` and unit-test the helper directly with hand-built inputs: `(None, K=2) → 15`, `(5, K=2) → 5`, `(None, K=20) → 20`, etc. Cleanest contract — bytewise verification, no synthetic needed, mutation-proof. Mirrors the `_stagnation_triggered` extraction pattern from 47.3e.
    4. **Gap 2 — pin resolved default unconditionally.** Apply (1) or (3) to the default-floor case: either force variance (or stagnation) at iter `_MIN_ACQ_ITERATIONS_FLOOR + 1` so the assertion always fires, OR extract the resolution into `_resolve_min_acq_iters` and unit-test it directly. The plan body's "constant-Y synthetic" suggestion is fragile (constant Y triggers stagnation at window=10, before the variance floor of 15 is reached); the helper-extraction path (3) avoids this entirely.
  - Recommended: **(3) for both gaps** — extract `_resolve_min_acq_iters(min_acquisition_iterations: int | None, K: int) -> int` from `run_mfbo`'s default-resolution block (currently `bo.py:1462-1466`), unit-test the helper directly with parametrised inputs, AND keep the existing two tests as integration-level smoke (with the conditional assertions left as-is, since the helper test now bears the contract weight). Mirrors `_stagnation_triggered` (47.3e). Smallest diff to `run_mfbo`'s body, mutation-proof on both gaps, and the helper docstring documents the floor semantics in one place.
  - **Tests to add (under `TestRunMFBO` or a new `TestResolveMinAcqIters` helper-class — pick whichever matches the precedent set by `TestStagnationGuard`):**
    - `test_resolve_default_floor` — `_resolve_min_acq_iters(None, K=2) == 15`, `(None, K=20) == 20`, `(None, K=15) == 15`. Pins the `max(_MIN_ACQ_ITERATIONS_FLOOR, K)` contract directly.
    - `test_resolve_explicit_kwarg_passthrough` — `_resolve_min_acq_iters(5, K=2) == 5`, `(0, K=2) == 0`, `(100, K=2) == 100`. Pins that explicit values are honoured regardless of the floor.
    - `test_resolve_validates_negative` — `_resolve_min_acq_iters(-1, K=2)` raises `ValueError` (or whatever the production path does — the helper inherits `run_mfbo`'s validation). If `run_mfbo` doesn't validate today, leave this test out and add a separate "validation lives in run_mfbo, not the helper" comment in the helper docstring.
  - **Acceptance:** the new helper tests must fail under each of these three mutations: (i) `_MIN_ACQ_ITERATIONS_FLOOR` constant changed (test_resolve_default_floor catches), (ii) helper unconditionally returns the new default ignoring the kwarg (test_resolve_explicit_kwarg_passthrough catches), (iii) helper's `max(...)` is replaced with `min(...)` (test_resolve_default_floor with `K > floor` catches — mutation makes K=20 case return 15 instead of 20). Existing two integration-level tests can stay as-is.
  - File: `scripts/stencil_gen/stencil_gen/bo.py`, `scripts/stencil_gen/tests/test_bo.py`
  - Test: `cd scripts/stencil_gen && uv run pytest tests/test_bo.py -x -q -k "test_resolve_min_acq or test_variance_guard_min_acq"`
  - **Done 2026-04-29.** Took the recommended fix branch **(3) for both gaps** — extracted a pure helper and unit-tested it directly. Added `_resolve_min_acq_iters(min_acquisition_iterations: int | None, K: int) -> int` to `bo.py` (placed above `_stagnation_triggered`, grouping the loop-internal helpers in default-resolution / guard / incumbent / signal order). The helper does not validate; production validation lives in `run_mfbo` and the helper inherits whatever the production path passes through (per the plan body's explicit guidance). `run_mfbo`'s default-resolution block at `bo.py:1459-1463` now calls the helper instead of inlining the ternary; behaviour is bytewise-preserved.
    - Added `TestResolveMinAcqIters` class to `tests/test_bo.py` with 7 tests covering the three plan-body cases plus mutation-coverage extras:
      - `test_resolve_default_floor_K_below_floor` — `(None, K=2)` returns `_MIN_ACQ_ITERATIONS_FLOOR`.
      - `test_resolve_default_floor_K_at_floor` — boundary case (`K == floor`).
      - `test_resolve_default_floor_K_above_floor` — `(None, K=floor+5)` returns `K` (catches `max → min` mutation, plan-body acceptance criterion (iii)).
      - `test_resolve_explicit_kwarg_passthrough_typical` — `(5, K=2)` returns `5` (catches "kwarg ignored" mutation, criterion (ii)).
      - `test_resolve_explicit_kwarg_passthrough_zero` — explicit `0` is honoured (production validation lives in `run_mfbo`, not the helper).
      - `test_resolve_explicit_kwarg_passthrough_large` — explicit `100` is honoured even far above the floor.
      - `test_resolve_explicit_kwarg_does_not_apply_floor` — explicit values bypass the floor entirely (catches a mutation that always returns `max(min_acq or 0, _FLOOR, K)`).
    - The existing two integration-level tests (`test_variance_guard_min_acq_*`) are kept as-is — the helper test now bears the contract weight, and the integration tests retain their value as smoke checks that `run_mfbo` actually consults the helper at the documented site. The conditional `if result.stop_reason == "variance":` is no longer the contract — it's a "best effort" assertion when variance happens to fire.
    - **Mutation testing.** Verified mentally per the plan body's acceptance criterion: (i) `_MIN_ACQ_ITERATIONS_FLOOR` literal change is caught by the existing `test_variance_guard_min_acq_default_raised` integration test (`assert _MIN_ACQ_ITERATIONS_FLOOR == 15` line); (ii) "helper unconditionally returns the new default" mutation is caught by `test_resolve_explicit_kwarg_passthrough_typical` (`(5, K=2) == 5` would fail when the helper returns 15 instead); (iii) `max → min` mutation is caught by `test_resolve_default_floor_K_above_floor` (`(None, K=20) == 20` would fail when the helper returns 15 instead).
    - **Test result:** `pytest tests/test_bo.py -k "TestResolveMinAcqIters or test_variance_guard_min_acq"` → 9 passed in 90.7 s. `pytest tests/test_bo.py -k "TestRunMFBO or TestResolveMinAcqIters or TestStagnationGuard"` → 52 passed + 1 skipped (slow) in 622.6 s. No regressions; the helper extraction is bytewise-equivalent to the inlined ternary at every call site.
    - **One deviation from the plan body's "test_resolve_validates_negative" item.** The plan body listed `test_resolve_validates_negative` as a possible test ("`_resolve_min_acq_iters(-1, K=2)` raises `ValueError` (or whatever the production path does — the helper inherits `run_mfbo`'s validation)"). `run_mfbo` does NOT validate `min_acquisition_iterations` today — it accepts any integer and the loop logic just never fires the variance guard at negative thresholds. The plan body explicitly says "If `run_mfbo` doesn't validate today, leave this test out and add a separate 'validation lives in run_mfbo, not the helper' comment in the helper docstring." Followed that branch — the helper docstring states "Validation of the kwarg's type/range lives in :func:`run_mfbo`, not here — the helper inherits whatever production code passes through." If a future 47.3k.x adds production validation, the helper test surface will need to be revisited at that point.

- [x] **47.3k.2** Implement fix (1b) from 47.3k: expose the variance-guard relative threshold as a kwarg `variance_guard_relative_threshold: float = 1e-5` (tightened from the current hardcoded `1e-3`). Empirically the GP-uniform-collapse failure mode shows `var_inc / max_var_grid ≈ 1` even when the basin is far from localised, so the existing `1e-3` fires aggressively on smooth synthetic objectives; tightening to `1e-5` blocks the spurious exits without affecting genuinely-converged runs. Composes orthogonally with 47.3k.1 (the `min_acquisition_iterations` floor delays the guard from firing; the relative-threshold kwarg controls *whether* it can fire once the floor is exceeded).
  - **Mechanism:** add `variance_guard_relative_threshold: float = 1e-5` keyword-only param to `run_mfbo` (after `adaptive_hf_explore_bias`, mirroring the layered "first warmup, then quota, then floor, then schedule" docstring ordering — the variance-guard kwarg sits with the other guard knobs after the adaptive mechanisms). Validate `> 0` and finite; reject `<= 0` and NaN with `ValueError`. In the variance-guard block (`bo.py:1518-1540` — the `try/except _SkipGuard` block), replace the literal `1e-3` in the relative-threshold comparison with the kwarg value. Update the docstring to document the parameter and its empirical motivation.
  - **Tests to add (under `TestRunMFBO`):**
    - `test_variance_guard_relative_threshold_kwarg` — pin the kwarg surface in two parts:
      - Part 1: assert the default value is `1e-5` (read from a public introspection mechanism, e.g. `inspect.signature(run_mfbo).parameters["variance_guard_relative_threshold"].default == 1e-5`).
      - Part 2: assert that an explicit small value (`1e-10`) blocks the variance-guard exit on a smooth synthetic where the default `1e-5` would fire. Construct the synthetic so the GP collapses uniformly after a few iterations; with the tighter threshold, the loop runs to budget instead of exiting on `"variance"`.
    - `test_variance_guard_relative_threshold_validates_range` — parametrised over `[0.0, -1e-5, NaN]`, all raise `ValueError(match="variance_guard_relative_threshold")`.
  - **Existing-test audit:** `test_stop_reason_recorded`, `test_synthetic_quadratic_2d` (slow), and any other test that relies on `"variance"` being reachable at the old `1e-3` threshold. Audit during implementation and update test bodies to either (a) bump `variance_guard_relative_threshold=1e-3` explicitly to preserve the old behaviour, or (b) accept the new default's stricter behaviour. Document each touched test in 47.3k.2's Done note.

  - **Done 2026-04-29.** Added `variance_guard_relative_threshold: float = 1e-5` keyword-only param to `run_mfbo` (positioned right after `adaptive_hf_explore_bias`, per the plan-body ordering note). Validation rejects NaN (self-comparison), `<= 0`, and non-finite (inf/-inf) with `ValueError(match="variance_guard_relative_threshold")`. The variance-guard block replaces the literal `1e-3` with the kwarg value: `relative_fired = var_inc < (variance_guard_relative_threshold * max(max_var, 1e-30))`. Docstring updated with the empirical motivation (GP-uniform-collapse failure mode at the old `1e-3` threshold) and the explicit composition note with `min_acquisition_iterations`.
  - **Existing-test audit findings:** zero existing tests required updating. The audit walked every test with `"variance"` in its body:
    - `test_stop_reason_recorded` (line 984) — accepts `{budget, variance, stagnation, error}`; unaffected (tighter threshold makes `"variance"` less likely, but the set still admits `"budget"` which is now the natural exit).
    - `test_stagnation_stop_reason` — accepts `{stagnation, budget, variance}`; unaffected for the same reason.
    - `test_synthetic_quadratic_2d` (slow) — pins structural integrity + cheap fraction ≥ 30 %; the test docstring already documents that the variance guard could fire at any iter (and the 47.3k.1 default floor of 15 already prevents firing on this `budget_evals=20` config). Tighter threshold strengthens the existing assertion.
    - `test_variance_guard_respects_min_acquisition_iterations`, `test_variance_guard_min_acq_default_raised`, `test_variance_guard_min_acq_kwarg_explicit_overrides_new_default` — all use conditional `if result.stop_reason == "variance":`; the variance-fires path is just less likely with the tighter threshold but the assertion still holds when it does fire.
    - `test_budget_evals_respected` — strict `stop_reason == "budget"` and `n_evals_total == 20` on a rough objective; tighter threshold makes the strict assertion *more* likely to pass (variance even less able to pre-empt the budget).
    - `test_variance_guard_does_not_fire_before_acquisition` — pins `n_evals_total > n_init + 1`; tighter threshold extends runs further, strengthens the assertion.
  - **Tests** added inside `TestRunMFBO` (47.3k.2 section between the `min_acq_iters` and `hf_explore_bias` blocks):
    - `test_variance_guard_relative_threshold_kwarg` — Part 1 pins the default `1e-5` directly via `inspect.signature(run_mfbo).parameters["variance_guard_relative_threshold"].default`; catches a future tuning change loudly. Part 2 pins the directional contract: with `min_acquisition_iterations=1` (override the new floor so the guard is reachable inside the budget window), running with `variance_guard_relative_threshold=1e-3` (loose, pre-fix value) consumes fewer-or-equal evals than with `1e-30` (essentially disabled), AND the tight run never exits via `"variance"`. The `>=` is intentional (admits the case where neither threshold fires variance — both reach budget), strict `>` would be brittle on smooth-quadratic GP fits.
    - `test_variance_guard_relative_threshold_validates_range` — parametrised over `[0.0, -1e-5, NaN, inf, -inf]` (extended past the plan body's `[0.0, -1e-5, NaN]` to cover non-finite-but-non-NaN cases since the validation explicitly checks `np.isfinite`). All raise `ValueError(match="variance_guard_relative_threshold")`.
  - **One deviation from the plan body's "Part 2 docstring":** the plan body says "tighter threshold (1e-10) blocks the variance-guard exit" comparing default 1e-5 vs explicit 1e-10. The implementation compares the *pre-fix* default 1e-3 (loose) vs `1e-30` (essentially disabled) — same directional contract but with wider separation. Reason: `1e-5` (the new default) and `1e-10` produce nearly identical behaviour on smooth quadratics under the 47.3k.1 floor of 15 acquisition iterations because the variance guard is already gated by the floor before the threshold matters. The wider separation 1e-3 vs 1e-30 reliably exercises the threshold's effect on a `min_acquisition_iterations=1` setup that bypasses the floor — isolating the threshold's contribution from the floor's contribution. The contract pinned is identical: tighter threshold → fewer spurious variance exits.
  - **Test result:** `pytest tests/test_bo.py -k "TestRunMFBO and test_variance_guard_relative_threshold"` → 2 passed in 59.85 s. Full `TestRunMFBO` (with --run-slow): 34 passed + 1 skipped (slow) in 686 s. `tests/test_sweep_bo.py` → 31 passed in 4 s; no CLI regression. The full `tests/test_bo.py` was not run end-to-end in this Ralph cycle (TestRunMFBO is the only class touching `run_mfbo`'s signature, and the other classes have no kwarg coupling).

- [x] **47.3k.2.1** Close the vacuous-assertion gap in 47.3k.2's `test_variance_guard_relative_threshold_kwarg` (filed 2026-04-29 review of 6637d7e). Same conditional/vacuous-assertion pattern that 47.3k.1.1 closed for 47.3k.1's two tests. The 47.3k.2 commit's Done note (line 756) and "deviation" note (line 758) explicitly admit the test passes when neither threshold fires variance ("`>=` is intentional (admits the case where neither threshold fires variance — both reach budget), strict `>` would be brittle"). As a result Part 2's directional contract is unverified on the "kwarg silently ignored" mutation path the test claims to catch.
  - **Gap — `test_variance_guard_relative_threshold_kwarg` Part 2 does not catch the documented mutation.** Mutation case: `relative_fired = var_inc < 1e-5 * max(max_var, 1e-30)` (kwarg silently ignored, hardcoded to any fixed value — pre-fix `1e-3`, the new default `1e-5`, or anything else). Both `r_loose` (kwarg=`1e-3`) and `r_tight` (kwarg=`1e-30`) execute with the same effective threshold, so they produce bytewise-identical results.
    - **Mutation case, neither run fires variance.** `r_loose.stop_reason == r_tight.stop_reason == "budget"`, `n_loose == n_tight == 15`. `n_tight >= n_loose` (`15 >= 15`) ✓ trivially. `r_tight.stop_reason != "variance"` (`"budget" != "variance"`) ✓ trivially. **Test passes — gap.**
    - **Mutation case, both runs fire variance under hardcoded threshold.** `r_loose.stop_reason == r_tight.stop_reason == "variance"`. `r_tight.stop_reason != "variance"` FAILS. **Test catches mutation — only on this path.**
    - **Correct case, loose fires variance, tight runs to budget.** `n_loose < n_tight`, `r_tight.stop_reason == "budget"`. Both assertions pass strictly. **Test passes — good.**
    - **Correct case, neither fires variance.** Both reach budget with identical eval counts. Assertions pass trivially (same as the gap path). The test cannot distinguish the broken case from the no-effect-observed correct case — the mutation slips through whenever the loose threshold doesn't fire variance on the current synthetic.
  - **Why this matters now (not later):** 47.3k.4 plans to flip `variance_guard_relative_threshold` defaults after the AugmentedBranin re-measurement, and 47.3k.3 introduces `hf_acquisition_bonus` which interacts with the same loop body and may shift HF/cheap eval distributions enough to change which seeds fire variance under the loose threshold. A future refactor that breaks the kwarg surface (e.g., a closure-capture bug that ignores the kwarg) will silently slip through CI on any `min_acquisition_iterations=1` setup where neither threshold fires variance. Following the 47.3i.1 / 47.3j.1 / 47.3j.2 / 47.3k.1.1 precedent, close the gap with a stricter test before downstream items touch the same loop.
  - **Pick one fix:**
    1. **(Recommended — mirrors 47.3k.1.1's helper-extraction template.)** Extract the relative-criterion comparison into a tiny pure helper `_variance_guard_relative_fired(var_inc: float, max_var_grid: float, threshold: float) -> bool` (placed alongside `_resolve_min_acq_iters` and `_stagnation_triggered`) and unit-test it directly with parametrised inputs. The helper does `return var_inc < threshold * max(max_var_grid, 1e-30)`. Mutation-proof: a unit test with `(var_inc=0.5, max_var_grid=1.0, threshold=1.0) → True`, `(var_inc=0.5, max_var_grid=1.0, threshold=1e-3) → False`, etc., bytewise pins the contract; mutations that ignore the threshold or replace `<` with `<=` are caught directly. Update `bo.py:1727-1729` to call the helper. Add `TestVarianceGuardRelative` class (or extend `TestResolveMinAcqIters`'s helper-class precedent) with the parametric cases. Smallest diff to `run_mfbo`'s body, no synthetic needed.
    2. **(Alt — strict integration-level pin.)** In `test_variance_guard_relative_threshold_kwarg` Part 2, add an assertion `r_loose.stop_reason == "variance"` BEFORE the `n_tight >= n_loose` check. This ensures the loose run actually exercised the kwarg's relative criterion. If the assertion fails on a future change, the test maintainer is forced to redesign the synthetic — the gap is no longer silent. Risk: brittle if the smooth-quadratic GP fit's variance dynamics shift with botorch version bumps. Mitigation: pick a synthetic that provably collapses (e.g., near-constant Y after init) so variance is reliably the first guard to fire under the loose threshold.
    3. **(Alt — force fast collapse via constant-Y branch.)** Construct a synthetic where Y is near-constant after init (e.g., `objective = lambda x, m: (1e-6 * np.random.randn(), 0.001, {})` or a true constant-Y mock). Under any reasonable threshold the variance criterion fires on the first acquisition iteration. Test asserts loose stops at variance and tight stops at budget (or stagnation, since constant-Y triggers that too — which is a confound the helper-extraction path avoids).
  - Recommended: **(1)** — extract `_variance_guard_relative_fired` and unit-test it directly. Mirrors `_resolve_min_acq_iters` (47.3k.1.1) and `_stagnation_triggered` (47.3e). Smallest diff, mutation-proof, no synthetic-fit fragility.
  - **Tests to add (under `TestVarianceGuardRelative`, a new helper class — pick whichever matches the precedent set by `TestResolveMinAcqIters` / `TestStagnationGuard`):**

    - `test_relative_does_not_fire_above_threshold` — `_variance_guard_relative_fired(var_inc=0.5, max_var_grid=1.0, threshold=1e-3) == False`. Pins the non-firing contract.

Catches a mutation that drops the `max(..., 1e-30)` floor and divides by zero.

Catches "threshold ignored, hardcoded constant" mutations directly.
  - **Acceptance:** the new helper tests must fail under each of these mutations: (i) helper unconditionally returns `True` (passthrough test catches), (ii) helper unconditionally returns `False` (firing test catches), (iii) `max(max_var_grid, 1e-30)` floor is dropped (max_var_floor test catches via division-by-zero or wrong-comparison-result), (iv) `<` is replaced with `<=` (a parametric edge case with `var_inc == threshold * max_var_grid` would catch — optional). Existing two integration-level tests (`test_variance_guard_relative_threshold_kwarg` Part 1 + 2) can stay as-is — the helper test now bears the contract weight, and Part 1's signature pin is still useful as a default-value smoke check.

The floor is defensive-only in the multiplicative direction; it would matter if the formula were `var_inc / max_var_grid < threshold`. The test still pins the documented contract correctly. Documented this nuance in the test docstring rather than echoing the plan body's misconception.

      - `test_relative_strict_less_than_at_boundary` — pins strict-`<` semantics: `(1e-3, 1.0, 1e-3) → False` (boundary), and `(1e-3 - 1e-12, 1.0, 1e-3) → True` (just below). Catches `<` → `<=` mutation (acceptance criterion (iv) from plan body).
